<h2>All Reviews</h2>

<ol>
    <li> This would be a great product if they take the mini saws off the edges. Those things slice through tender skin like it is butter. The shaver part works great but is almost impossible to use because of the saws on both sides. I guess they thought this is a hedge trimmer.</li>
    <li> The battery quickly degraded after a few months and the head broke, so the cutter wouldn&#x27;t stay attached the warranty process wasn&#x27;t worth it.</li>
    <li> This groomer is not recommended. It does well on arms, chest, legs. It will however, pull and cut your private area. Once again - move on, this is not the one for you. UPDATE: I needed a new blade attachement. Threw this one away and bought a BG2028. The newer model and blade work fantastic. No cuts or scary groin bleeding yet :)</li>
    <li> I purchased one of these in 2011.  My observations are that the clipper extensions were extraordinarily difficult to put on and off -- and I was alway afraid of breaking them because they were plastic.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After 25 or so uses over 2 and a half years the on/off button wore out.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I did not think it was particularly well built and I am going to try a different brand now.</li>
    <li> The performance of this device is as in other reviews:  it works quite well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;However, this model is notorious for a design flaw where the plastic head that holds the foil (aka the blade assembly) can become loose and unable to hold the foil in place.  Some people never have this problem, but I was one of the unlucky ones -after about a year (~10 uses), the plastic head was no longer able to hold the foil in place, rendering the device unusable.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Well, the other day I finally got around to digging up the warranty/instruction booklet, and the device is under a two-year warranty.  I called Phillips&#x27; warranty center and they were able to identify my unit /w just the information on the device itself (didn&#x27;t need my receipt or the UPC code I had cut out &amp; saved).  I got a representative quickly on the line, and she arranged for a replacement plastic head to be sent.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I got the package about a week and a half later, and it was the wrong part -they sent me a replacement foil.  So I call in again (this time they only needed my phone #) and explain the issue.  The representative was very apologetic, and looked into the issue further.  Turns out, they no longer are able to supply the plastic head component of the device, so they went ahead and arranged for a new unit (/w a tag in it to return the old defective one to them) to be sent to me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Although the mistake was kind of annoying, I did get a free foil out of it, and am getting a new unit in the end, so I&#x27;m pretty happy.  As long as you&#x27;re covered by warranty (and don&#x27;t destroy the device yourself), it seems they&#x27;re a decent company who will take care of their customers, at least for these types of lifestyle products.</li>
    <li> Would recommend for any guys wanting to trim down for a neater appearance. I had 60 years of growth that now looks trimmed and neat. Just like getting a haircut. My wife likes the new look. Used the number one attachment for most of my body and no attachment for under arms and intimates.</li>
    <li> I agree with most posts on here, the attachments are hard to use, but it does do the job. One thing to point out is mine stopped working with only about 2 uses per month after about 18 months. I have \\&quot;refreshed\\&quot; the batteries 3 times now (fully drain, recharge, fully drain) and I still only get a few minutes of \\&quot;full power\\&quot; before it goes about 1/2 speed for the rest of the charge. I&#x27;m going to try one more unit, but I&#x27;m getting a SquareTrade Warranty this time in case it has the same battery trouble.</li>
    <li> Works very well. I did not get one nick or cut when shaving those sensitive areas. The only downside I found is that the detachable combs are a little tricky to get on and off.</li>
    <li> It is very rare I find a product that I so strongly dislike and well this is it. I purchased this product a few years back and found that although it was crafted cleverly to appeal on the eye and look good it was far from that. I found that simply cutting long body hairs in simple places became a choir for this groomer or it just painfully pulled hair right out. This often caused the head of the trimmer to fill up or even pop off. Regardless, I purchased this product to remove hair from the back and neck and well after about 6 uses too many this product became a resident of my garbage can. If you have thick hair or pain sensories in your skin...avoid using this product and pick up a Remington or a regular Conair hair trimmer to get the job done.</li>
    <li> This thing works better that I had hoped especially in the very sensitive male areas and underarms. It worked flawlessly! I was so impressed I got brave and trimmed my long chest &amp; stomach hair using the length control attachments. Again the results were excellent. I got braver still and did my arms and legs experimenting with the different lengths. When I was done with that, I got the bravest yet and did my eyebrows and it worked great. I&#x27;m thrilled I bought this. Luckily it came up on my Amazon recommendations and I bought it because I was sick of poor results and cuts from a cordless Subeam clipper I was using.</li>
    <li> i am a woman, and i bought this men&#x27;s electric shaver to use on my legs, underarms, and bikini area. the main reason why i bought it was because i have a mangled leg from an accident, and i found it hard to shave around all the bumps, ridges and scars with a disposable. it works fine, but not as smooth as a cheap disposable razor. you can actually feel it pulling the hairs...not terribly painful, but i can feel it. it has not cut me once since ive been using it, for about a month now. i am happy with it.</li>
    <li> This is a great shaver. I&#x27;ve used it so far on my chest, back, and underarms and it has done a wonderful job. I bought it from amazon for $30. Definitely worth the price!</li>
    <li> I know the title can be a little confusing so let me explain.  The motor on the razor is really good and the razor itself is very ergonomical.  And its great that its waterproof.      Now the bad.  The replaceable razor foils are cheap and very poorly engineered.  I have had several break on me and actually scratch my skin.  The foils will sometimes push down inside the little plastic piece that holds them together.  Once they ever bend a little like that they are useless.  I have actually messed up a foil taking off the guard before...ugh!  They arent cheap either, about $10 a piece.      If they made some better foils this would be great but the foils just ruin it for me.</li>

    <li> I will be completely honest; I been out of the game so to speak and this weekend, I will be having an experience where this thing is needed lol I just wanted to say this shaver is completely amazing and definitely a 5 star product. I used the Balla Powder Talc for men,the one with the fragrance, was great and absolutely no itching :D which I am happy about; and other reviews have said the foil is very fragile, and while that may be true I am not worried as it is easy to replace and very cheap at that matter so I am assured when I need to replace it I will have no troubles. Thank you so much Philips for making this shaver. I am very pleased, especially me being 18 and in College yeah I am glad to have this and it arrived perfectly packaged, everything there and even charged already so I couldn&#x27;t be happier.        If anyone has any questions I would be glad to answer them :)    Reviewed by- Jacob Freeman    [[ASIN:B000VLH8W6 Balla Powder Talc For Men, Original 100 g]]</li>
    <li> There are already nearly 800 reviews of this product so it is highly unlikely that I can substantively offer much to the discussion which has already been had, but, I&#x27;ll put in my two-cents nonetheless.  As a bodybuilder, I like to keep a \\&quot;clean\\&quot; look.  I picked this shaver up from Target for about $10 more than it is listed here (at the time of this review), mostly because I wanted to (finally) try it out and thought it might serve as an alternative to waxing.    First - no, it&#x27;s not an alternative to waxing.  It does leave stubble.    Second - there is no way I would (a) take this anywhere above the neckline and, more importantly, (b) take this thing anywhere below the belt-line.  The product manual indicates that you should not use it above the neck, but I mention it because others seemingly have used it on their face/head.  Again, whether the manual said anything about it or not, I still would never do it.  While I suffered no cuts or gashes (as others seemingly have), it did \\&quot;pull\\&quot; and \\&quot;tug\\&quot; a bit while doing my chest, back, underarms, etc.  It was not painful per se, but it was definitely momentarily uncomfortable and raised serious doubts about venturing further south.  Nay, for points south, I will stick to using [[ASIN:B001G7PTVQ Gillette Mach3 Disposable, Sensitive, 3-Count (Pack of 2)]] or [[ASIN:B003U4CJT8 Bic Flex 4 - 1 Pack]] with some [[ASIN:B003I87A2M Gillette Comfort Advantage Shave Gel (4 pack)]].    Third - I tried this both dry and wet.  While it is a somewhat nice idea that this can be taken in the shower, it is not altogether practical.  Hairs have a tendency to stick to the body when wet and, unless you use some manner of light soap/shave cream/shave gel, sliding this thing across a wet body is not as easy as it is while dry.  Using this dry is definitely a better alternative.  I also found the attachments to be pretty much useless.  In addition, note that due to the short handle of this product, completely doing one&#x27;s back is a two-person job.  This is especially true for us bodybuilders; my arms are large and reaching around to the middle of my back is no easy task...if not impossible.    Fourth - in fairness, for the most part, it does what it says it will do, but I can&#x27;t help but feel there are better options out there. This will be going back.    All in all,    Not recommended.</li>
    <li> You get what you pay for with this thing. I plan on trying the Remington BHT-2000 body shaver in the next month or two and will compare that unit against this one.      ***UPDATE***      I recently purchased the Remington BHT-2000 body shaver and have reviewed it.  Here&#x27;s is an updated review comparing the Noreclo to the Remington:    To begin, I find the Remington to be more solidly built than the Bodygroom. Plus, the Remington&#x27;s smaller design makes it easier to maneuver around the groin area than the Bodygroom for trimming that area. Advantage: Remington. I like how the Remington has a dial-type head (similar to what you see in most beard trimmers) in which you can choose from 5 setting for hair trimming. Advantage: Remington    Thirdly, I found the shaving capability of the Remington to be quite poor compared to the Norelco. For either unit, it is recommended to trim the hair to the lowest setting before attempting to shave using the foil head. If you don&#x27;t trim the hair first to as short as possible, the shaving head on each unit will not be able to shave the hair properly. Getting back to the review...the Remington dual head shaver attachment is unsatisfactory. It does not shave as close as the Norelco foil head, nor is it as irritation free as the Norelco foil head. I used the foil head on the Remington as gently as possible on both my testicles and part of the shaft, and I felt a stinging razor burn on two separate occasions. Eee-yowch. This did not happen with the Norelco Bodygroom. Advantage: Norelco.    I would recommend that if you plan to simply trim your groin area, then your best bet is to go with the Remington as it is the better trimmer. If your desire is to shave your groin area as smooth as possible with an electric instrument, than your best bet is to go with the Norelco Bodygroom as it is the better shaver. Please understand, however, that even with the Norelco being used as a shaver, you will not experience a shave as close as you would by using a blade.    Based on my experience, I find trimming the groin area to be the way to go instead of shaving the area. In order to keep the groin region hair free, you would have to shave that area every day. I find I can get by with trimming that area to a very short length once a week to keep it rather well maintained.</li>

    <li> This thing cut me up a bit... not as bad as previous electric trimmers/razors I tried, but it&#x27;s not quite as suited to \\&quot;sensitive areas\\&quot; as they say.  The problem is the top and bottom trimmer blades (the ones that are not under the foil) catch your skin (even when you&#x27;re trying to hold it taut), especially in concave areas.  There needs to be a way to turn them off independently of the blades under the foil, and/or the teeth should be much finer (like the little \\&quot;finishing touch\\&quot; shavers) so your skin won&#x27;t slip in between the teeth.    The blades under the foil did not irritate my skin and they made a pretty close shave.    Battery: There is no battery meter, and you&#x27;re not supposed to leave it in the charger 24/7 (because it&#x27;s NiMH), so there are issues not having enough charge to finish the job (until the next day after you charge it).     <li> Let&#x27;s start with this fact: the Philips Norelco BG2020 Bodygroom works great right out of the box. Just charge it up, slap on your preferred guard size, and start grooming. It gets to the hard to reach areas and, with some stretching, can even get the center of your back! It&#x27;s easy to use and easy to clean. No problems. Best trimmer of its kind.     The issue comes when you&#x27;ve had the groomer for six months or more. If you have to change guards often (as in, you want to use #1 for \\&quot;the boys\\&quot;, but #2 for the rest of your body, and #3 for calves and forearms). The guards snap onto the groomer using a notch-and-nub system that, for a time, works great. But over time, after snapping on and off, these notches wear out. Eventually any amount of pressure on the tip of the guards will result in your guard popping off and BUZZ you get a big bald spot on your body.     It&#x27;s particularly annoying to be in the middle of a very visible area (like your chest) and have the guard pop off. The reward is a large spot that looks totally ridiculous. This is a design flaw that should be remedied with any future models. The guards need to be more secure... perhaps a slot on the sides upon which you slide the guards onto the unit?     Additionally, the rechargeable battery eventually loses steam after a few months of use. After a year of use, I am lucky to get 10 minutes of charge out of it. That makes grooming particularly inconvenient. I have to do it in stages. Chest one day, back another, and so on.     It would be nice if a) you could buy new guards separately from the unit (in the even that you lose them or they wear down as described above) and b) if you could buy a new battery for the groomer.     Overall, I will buy another Bodygroom Shaver, but I do it begrudgingly with the knowledge that I will run into these issues again a year from now.</li>

Both positive and negative reviews can help people decide if a product might be for them, especially if they don&#x27;t associate themselves with a positive or negative reviewer. I write reviews because I have saved a lot of time and money by reading other people&#x27;s reviews. Do a civic duty and help other customers; write a review.</li>

    <li> After a year of a good grooming, the unit&#x27;s switch suddenly got stuck in the \\&quot;on\\&quot; position. Middle of the night, total silence in the house.. Except for what sounded like a huge vibrator. Had to shove it under a pillow and wait till the batteries died. Arrrgh.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now, how do you fix that? Pretty simple. The switch is getting stuck because of the vacuum developing inside of the watertight container. The unit is getting hot in the shower, pressure inside increases, and it (somehow) releases that pressure. Eventually, you are getting enough vacuum to suck the membrane that covers the switch almost all the way in. All you have to do to fix that is let some air in.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First, make sure the unit is dry in and out. Use a compressed air can to blow water drops out of hard to reach places if you have to. You don&#x27;t want to let any water get inside! Now, remove the head. Just pull it out.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Next, using a flathead screwdriver or utility knife, pull out those silvery colored side moldings. The case will open like a clamshell. You will find a fairly small watertight container with all of the electrical components inside. Carefully pull out any of the latches that are used to keep it closed. Pull two latches if that wasn&#x27;t enough; your on/off switch membrane will immediately \\&quot;pop\\&quot; back into shape.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Reseal the unit back like it was before. Works like new!</li>
